<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b03f2b83-1e30-47e0-aca7-c0d23d380c73'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer296370385884248627">Waverly and Kieran are finally reunited on the Empyrean. Kieran has led the boys safely up to this point, and now that the girls are back, their mission seems slightly less impossible: to chase down the New Horizon, and save their parents from the enemy ship. But nothing is truly as it seems…Kieran’s leadership methods have raised Seth’s hackles— and Waverly’s suspicions. </span>
  <span id="freeText296370385884248627" style="display:none">Waverly and Kieran are finally reunited on the Empyrean. Kieran has led the boys safely up to this point, and now that the girls are back, their mission seems slightly less impossible: to chase down the New Horizon, and save their parents from the enemy ship. But nothing is truly as it seems…Kieran’s leadership methods have raised Seth’s hackles— and Waverly’s suspicions. Is this really her fiancé? The handsome, loving boy she was torn from just a short time before? More and more, she finds her thoughts aligned with Seth’s. But if Seth is Kieran’s Enemy No. 1, what does that make her? <br /><br />In one night, a strange explosion rocks the Empyrean—shooting them off course and delaying their pursuit of the New Horizon—and Seth is mysteriously released from the brig. Seth is the most obvious suspect for the explosion, and Waverly the most obvious suspect for releasing him. As the tension reaches a boiling point, will Seth be able to find the true culprit before Kieran locks them both away—or worse? Will Waverly follow her heart, even if it puts lives at risk? With the balance of power precarious and the clock ticking, every decision counts… every step brings them closer to a new beginning, or a sudden end...</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_435346365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/435346365" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/435346365?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447208051" href="/book/show/15780722-spark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=creepy-love-triangle">creepy-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2012">reviewed-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cliffhanger-ending">cliffhanger-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=multiple-povs">multiple-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=moments-of-great-frustration">moments-of-great-frustration</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer435346365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2138741304334798818"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/>Unsettling, grim, nerve-wracking, action-packed, frightening, riveting, enthralling, intelligent, fast-paced, claustrophobic, eerie, appalling, passionate… Any one of these words can be used to describe Spark, and yet, not even all of them put together come close to explaining the all-consuming thrill ride that is this book. Amy Kathleen Ryan achieved something not many authors can: Spark is one of those highly adaptable books that can be read one way by a younger audience, and complete</span>
  <span id="freeText2138741304334798818" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br>Unsettling, grim, nerve-wracking, action-packed, frightening, riveting, enthralling, intelligent, fast-paced, claustrophobic, eerie, appalling, passionate… Any one of these words can be used to describe Spark, and yet, not even all of them put together come close to explaining the all-consuming thrill ride that is this book. Amy Kathleen Ryan achieved something not many authors can: Spark is one of those highly adaptable books that can be read one way by a younger audience, and completely differently by someone older. Behind the exciting story are layers and layers of psychology and current issues that can be discussed for hours on end. <br><br>Spark picks up exactly where Glow left off. The girls are back on the Empyrean, but all they did by returning was replace one religious tyrant with another. Kieran is leading the ship with sermons, lies and deceptions, and not even his ex fiancé can stand in his way. Weaverly has more enemies than she can count, both on Empyrean and the New Horizon, and Seth has lost everything when Kieran took over. <br><br><b>
  <i>She’d been through too much. Some part of her had snapped. Her humanity had gone on hiatus, and what was left behind was her animal instinct: kill, hurt, maim, survive.</i>
</b> <br><br>There are no heroes in Spark. Each of these characters exist in a moral gray area, and Kieran, who started out as a classic hero in Glow, turned into something entirely different. The most frightening thing about him is his firm belief that he is right, that he is being led by God and that, as God’s chosen vessel, he can do no wrong. Weaverly and Seth are confronted with the impossibility of reasoning with someone like him while still trying to find the remnants of the person he used to be. <br><br>What makes Spark truly stand out is that Amy Kathleen Ryan doesn’t hide behind the age of her characters. She refuses to adapt, embellish or gloss over the ugly facts. There are some truly selfless and kind secondary characters because there have to be – there always are in life - but the leaders, our protagonists, are all power-hungry and selfish to the core. There’s nothing even remotely good in Kieran Alden anymore, and Weaverly Marshall is on the verge of insanity, crazed by her need for revenge. Oh, sure, Seth Ardvale had a change of heart and came to understand the error of his ways, but all that got him were a couple of fractured ribs and a place in the brig. <br><br><b><i>She’d known fear before, of course, but this terror at the end of her life had been new. It hollowed her out, debased her, turned her into nothing more than airless lungs and bloodless brain. A gray cloud had crept into the borders of her vision and a voice inside her had screamed, </i>I’m dying! I’m dying now!</b><br><br><br>And the situations they’re in are even more dangerous than last time. In Glow, the crew was fighting an external enemy and the disaster was of much bigger proportions, but that somehow made it less personal. In Spark, the kids of the Empyrean are mostly fighting each other, and as it turns out, there’s nothing more dangerous or cruel than a group of young people left to fend for themselves, especially when the kids in question are motivated almost entirely by revenge. Survival takes the back seat in Spark. Kieran and his crew are willing to sacrifice almost anything to get their parents back and inflict revenge on the crew of New Horizon. <br><br>Spark is obviously not for the faint-hearted. It gave me food for thought but, quite frankly, these aren’t things I enjoy thinking about. Who knows how any of us would behave in such conditions? <br>Extra brownie points go to Amy Kathleen Ryan for achieving the impossible and getting me out of my reading slump. Hurray! <br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2138741304334798818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319935803?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mimi by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/138065-crystal-allen">Crystal Allen</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=boys-i-wish-were-real">boys-i-wish-were-real</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=best-of-2012">best-of-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319935803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2791669625957129615"><b>Rating:</b> 4.5 otherworldly stars out of 5! <br/><br/>After not really loving <b>Glow</b> earlier this year, I went into the sequel with zero expectations. I started it thinking I'd be able to fit in a few chapters here and there, that I could put it down if I wanted to. But I was <i>completely</i> wrong! <br/><br/><b>Spark</b> was amazing from beginning to heart-stopping end! It picks up right where <b>Glow</b> left off, with all of the kids stuck on the spaceship alone, trying to reunite with their parents who were captive on another ship.Ther</span>
  <span id="freeText2791669625957129615" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> 4.5 otherworldly stars out of 5! <br /><br />After not really loving <b>Glow</b> earlier this year, I went into the sequel with zero expectations. I started it thinking I'd be able to fit in a few chapters here and there, that I could put it down if I wanted to. But I was <i>completely</i> wrong! <br /><br /><b>Spark</b> was amazing from beginning to heart-stopping end! It picks up right where <b>Glow</b> left off, with all of the kids stuck on the spaceship alone, trying to reunite with their parents who were captive on another ship.There's a little bit of deception, a lot of secrets, and enough mistrust to last a lifetime. It all makes everything on the Empyrean even more intense. <br /><br />I was so invested in this story that I found myself yelling out loud. When bad things happened, I curled up in a ball and prayed for the best. And when Kieran did something ridiculous, I imagined hitting him over the head with a stick. Repeatedly. <br /><br />(Seth was my favourite character, so everything Kieran did to him just made me so angry!) <br /><br />My heart ached for Waverly. Everyone wrongly blamed her for abandoning their parents, even though none of them would've made it out alive if she hadn't done what she did. She had to live with everyone's hatred and guilt everyday, but she still stayed strong and more clear-minded.. She was fifteen like I am, but I could never imagine being as strong as her! <br /><br />Actually, the <i>whole cast</i> continued to blow my mind. Over and over again, I reminded myself that they were just kids — that the oldest on the space ship was sixteen years old, and yet somehow they were surviving. They were intelligent and sneaky when they need to be, yet despite their brilliance, it was easy to see how real they were as kids. It was all believable.<br /><br />With an intensely unpredictable storyline and characters I couldn't stop rooting for, <b>Spark</b> was an amazing installment to the series that sure sets the bar high for the next! :) <br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> I would recommend this book whether you liked <b>Glow</b> or not! It was absolutely worth the sleepless night I got from wrongly believing it wouldn't be that addicting! ;)<br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.ca/2012/06/review-spark.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>)</span>

<div id="review_761557163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/761557163" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/761557163?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=books-that-linger">books-that-linger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761557163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9306662987886001209">Rating: 4.5 Stars<br/><br/>After <i>Glow</i> ripped my heart out, leaving me an emotional wreck, you’d think I’d have been a little more hesitant to crack open the spine of <i>Spark.</i> Not at all. I dove into this novel the first chance I had and refused to emerge until it was over, its last page taunting me with its promise of the “thrilling conclusion” to come Summer 2013. (Needless to say, that last page is a liar as <i>Flame</i> releases January 7th, 2014. I still cannot believe it had the audacity to throw into my face</span>
  <span id="freeText9306662987886001209" style="display:none">Rating: 4.5 Stars<br /><br />After <i>Glow</i> ripped my heart out, leaving me an emotional wreck, you’d think I’d have been a little more hesitant to crack open the spine of <i>Spark.</i> Not at all. I dove into this novel the first chance I had and refused to emerge until it was over, its last page taunting me with its promise of the “thrilling conclusion” to come Summer 2013. (Needless to say, that last page is a liar as <i>Flame</i> releases January 7th, 2014. I still cannot believe it had the audacity to throw into my face the fact that I still need to wait two months to find out what happens to these characters…two months!) Despite the stunning non-ending of <i>Spark,</i> leaving us on the precipice of immense change for the characters we’ve grown to hate and love, this vicious cliffhanger did, in no way, diminish my love for the novel as a whole. Avoiding Middle Book Syndrome spectacularly, <i>Spark</i> proves to be even more of a mind-fuck than its predecessor ever was. <br /><br />A month after the events of <i>Glow,</i> Seth still remains a prisoner in the brigs, Kieran the unlawful and un-elected Captain of the Empyrean, and Waverly the girl who left the adults behind on the New Horizon. Although the girls are finally back on the Empyrean, the tension has only escalated, causing Kieran to accelerate the rate of the ship and make frantic contact with Anne Mather to negotiate for the release of their parents. Then, a strange explosion occurs on the Empyrean, freeing Seth from his prison and making him the most obvious suspect. As the crew members soon discover, though, there is a New Horizon terrorist aboard the Empyrean. If that weren’t terrifying enough, Kieran has become consumed by his hunger for control, assuming the role of a dictator Waverly despises and vehemently opposes. As the Empyrean slowly tears itself apart from the inside, will they ever get the adults back? Or are they doomed to fall to the New Horizon…again?<br /><br />While the events of <i>Spark</i> never take place on the New Horizon, it is a scarier novel for it. Waverly, expecting to be safely back home on the Empyrean, finds her fiancée a changed man and the girls she worked to rescue an ungrateful lot. Thus, suffering under the trauma of her experiences on the New Horizon, the psychological damage slowly begins to grate. While Waverly attempts to create a democratic system of government aboard the Empyrean, lashing out at Kieran’s dictator behavior and vouching for the innocence of Seth, the vessel of the Empyrean becomes a battleground to win supporters. Team Waverly or Team Kieran?<br /><br />In many ways, this is a political struggle. It is evident to the crew that there will no longer be a wedding between Waverly and Kieran, but choosing between both stubborn individuals is a trial as well. And in politics, nothing is <i>quite</i> fair, just as corruption – of morals, of policies, of people – is at large. Moreover, the savageness of these children comes to light as they slowly destroy one another, their “leaders”, and their hope of survival. It is a brutal, horrible mess, reminding me of what the Hunger Games would have been like if, instead of arrows and knives, the weapons were vitriol and sarcasm. Ryan never bothers to shield her younger audience from these atrocities – which is refreshing. All too often, the plot or scope of a novel will demand difficult decisions that are withheld for the sake of the genre or marketing schemes, but Ryan never hesitates to unearth these realities.<br /><br />While Waverly is fighting her own inner – and outer – battle, struggling to take some control of a ship where Kieran rules, all while trying not to break down and lose her sanity, Kieran becomes increasingly unstable. Although he is still quick-thinking and intelligent, the religion he raises and his biased policies make him our new “villain.” Of course, there still remains so much gray matter when it comes to Kieran. We know what he’s been through and in an effort to contain hundreds of people – and meet their expectations – he resorts to cruelty. None of the situations these teens are placed in are easy, which make the tough decisions they take all the more plausible – and even forgiving. It is a double-edged sword, one that is difficult to think through. Are there even any villains on these ships anymore? I don’t know, which is both a scary thought and an intriguing one.<br /><br />While Seth never had a voice in <i>Glow,</i> he does in <i>Spark</i> which is an essential – and smart – tactical decision. As each of these perspectives remains in the third-person, there is no trouble discerning them from one another and I found Seth’s musings to be most interesting. After all the mistakes Seth committed in <i>Glow,</i> I find he is perhaps the most sane and morally correct individual in <i>Spark.</i> Unlike Waverly, Kieran, or the masses of secondary characters, he doesn’t seek to undermine, overthrow, or regain power. Instead, his sole goal is to redeem himself in the eyes of the Empyrean crew and, in particular, Waverly. While the romance in this novel is contained – easily – within a handful of lines, the affection Seth feels for Waverly is palpable, especially as it is in stark contrast with Kieran’s feelings. Although the relationship between Seth and Waverly is subtle, practically non-existent to a large degree, their friendship and understanding goes a long way.<br /><br /><i>Spark</i> is not a romance, but the small inclusion of true fondness hidden under all the savagery of these survivors was a pleasant glimmer of hope. Even the few tight friendships, the slow build-up of trust, and even the growth – psychological growth that led to a greater understanding of oneself – was written with feeling. While <i>Spark</i> is a more political, thought-provoking installment than its predecessor – and a stronger novel to be sure – this series as a whole is flawless, despite the flaws of its cast. I adore Ryan’s exploration of ambiguous morality throughout these books and for perhaps the first time, I truly cannot predict a single event in <i>Flame.</i> Will everyone continue to turn against one another, or will they finally band together? Who knows? After all, humanity has never been predictable.<br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2013/11/review-spark-by-amy-kathleen-ryan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9306662987886001209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17848957686813553285">Under normal circumstances i would have loved Seth but somehow the fact that everyone thinks that Kieran is a dictator changed my view. I am totally for justice and because of what Waverly thought about Kieran based on what Seth said pissed me off and also the fact that she thought that he was acting like Anne. <br/><br/>What annoys me the most is Waverly didnt trust Kieran.   <span id="freeText17848957686813553285" style="display:none">Under normal circumstances i would have loved Seth but somehow the fact that everyone thinks that Kieran is a dictator changed my view. I am totally for justice and because of what Waverly thought about Kieran based on what Seth said pissed me off and also the fact that she thought that he was acting like Anne. <br /><br />What annoys me the most is Waverly didnt trust Kieran. She decides that Seth is not evil but she doesn't realize that the reason Kieran turned into what he is, is because of Seth. How would she feel if someone locked her into a jail for no good reason and basically starved her, and how would she feel if everyone gave false statements about what happened to save their own asses. <br /><br />It's really depressing knowing that Kieran acted like this only because of his fear of something like that ever happening again (in my opinion at least). What Seth did to him left a permanent mental and physical scar (he mentions that he is still weak from his experience months afterwards). Despite trying to maintain his position as head, Kieran really did care about his people and he loved them. Seth and Waverly may not have been his favorites but can you blame him? Waverly accused him of being the bad guy and he freaking loved her, she broke his heart. Seth wanted to kill him.<br /><br />I wonder how its going to be like in the next book, but seriously I think its obvious she will be with Seth, but hey Kieran deserves a happy ending, he has gone through hell and right in the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ he saw that his mom was basically a puppet. <div id="review_381617456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381617456" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581282691p2/5501124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381617456?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=i-have-a-copy">i-have-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=review-on-the-blog">review-on-the-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=july-2012-release">july-2012-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381617456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3408329468854540848">Spark by Amy Kathleen Ryan is the second book in the Sky Chasers series. I reviewed book one, Glow, last week and really enjoyed it so I was keen to read the sequel and find out what happened next.<br/><br/>Spark picks up a month after the events of Glow. Seth Ardvale is in the brig on Kieran Alden’s orders as punishment for trying to kill him. Waverly Marshall hasn’t visited Seth since she arrived back on board but Kieran is still suspicious of her and orders another crew member to follow her and report </span>
  <span id="freeText3408329468854540848" style="display:none">Spark by Amy Kathleen Ryan is the second book in the Sky Chasers series. I reviewed book one, Glow, last week and really enjoyed it so I was keen to read the sequel and find out what happened next.<br /><br />Spark picks up a month after the events of Glow. Seth Ardvale is in the brig on Kieran Alden’s orders as punishment for trying to kill him. Waverly Marshall hasn’t visited Seth since she arrived back on board but Kieran is still suspicious of her and orders another crew member to follow her and report back to him. A series of problems occur on the ship resulting in Seth escaping the brig and realising something very important that he wants to share with Kieran but he has to be wary of being caught. Kieran is holding onto control of the ship by forcing his beliefs on his crew, promising to rescue their parents and he also has to deal with contact from Anne Mather, pastor of the New Horizons.<br /><br />We’re introduced to a third point of view in Spark and that is Seth’s. I think this was a great move on Amy’s behalf, as I wanted to get to know him and I found him to be more likeable than Kieran. Don’t get me started on Kieran! He’s the guy you’ll love to dislike. He’s let the control go to his head and now enjoys the attention that his sermons bring him. He’s also become quite paranoid and orders a young boy, Philip, to follow Waverly. Waverly is feeling guilty about abandoning their parents and has to deal with verbal abuse from the other kids on board so she keeps to herself most of the time and is not the girl she used to be.<br /><br />I found Glow to be intense and thrilling and I have to say Spark really upped the ante. There was an added element of danger to the already dire situation and I often felt my heart racing as I read. The thought of being locked on board a ship with so many places for people to hide but at the same time nowhere to run left me chilled and I was turning the pages as fast as I could.<br /><br />Like in Glow, things don’t always go to plan for these kids and I found that quite realistic and it meant that I never found the story predictable. It was great to get inside the minds of Seth and Waverly and see how they were changing, for better and for worse. Seth definitely grew on me and took the time to consider his previous behaviour. Waverly on the other hand has allowed the pain and suffering to get to her, changing her behaviour and making her hungry for revenge – something I could understand.<br /><br />Spark is a heart-stopping story of revenge and the perfect sequel to Glow. The cliff hanger ending has left me wishing that I could fast forward time to the release date of book three!<br /><br />Thank you to the lovely people at Pan Macmillan Australia for my review copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3408329468854540848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_284242528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/284242528" />
    <a title="Braiden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4317431-braiden"><img alt="Braiden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456556505p2/4317431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284242528?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Braiden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Braiden" href="/user/show/4317431-braiden">Braiden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284242528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8564193077307003244">4.5 stars. <br/><br/>I left Glow completely stunned and confused – there I was for the entire book despising Seth, then the entire ship gets flipped on its head and I’m unaware of who I should have been hating all along. Authors who are able to transform your perception of a character within a few sentences are rare; Amy Kathleen Ryan is one of those. This continued on into the sequel, Spark. For a good portion of the book I despised Kieran more and more as the pages flicked by and liked Seth in Spark mor</span>
  <span id="freeText8564193077307003244" style="display:none">4.5 stars. <br /><br />I left Glow completely stunned and confused – there I was for the entire book despising Seth, then the entire ship gets flipped on its head and I’m unaware of who I should have been hating all along. Authors who are able to transform your perception of a character within a few sentences are rare; Amy Kathleen Ryan is one of those. This continued on into the sequel, Spark. For a good portion of the book I despised Kieran more and more as the pages flicked by and liked Seth in Spark more than I did Kieran in Glow. Ryan just has a knack for writing fantastic characters no matter their ability to instill love or hate in you.<br /><br /><blockquote>If he ever did get out of here, he’d show her he could be a good person. It didn’t matter that he could never have her. He just couldn’t stand the thought of her thinking badly of him. And maybe, just maybe, he could help her, too. Because whatever had happened to her on the New Horizon had pulled her downward, bent her back, hollowed out her eyes. If he could see her again, he’d take nothing from her. He wanted nothing. He just wanted to help—be a friend.</blockquote><br /><br />The above quote from Seth just presents the transformation that occurs in him within the first couple of chapters from his POV… but I must say, it felt like Ryan has two different styles of writing for two groups of characters: those that we are made to side with and like and those that we are meant to dislike and wish would see the light – or just die. This was probably why I liked Seth more than Kieran in Spark, but if that logic is bizarre from your view then it must be something else. Having liked Seth more than Kieran I should have enjoyed Spark more than its predecessor, but that wasn’t case; maybe I would have if I reread Glow with a different perception, knowing where book two was going. Both books are equally as good, the first focusing more on religion, the second more on politics – and both involve ceaseless morality dilemmas, which I think in Spark was upped the ante. The morality really showed all sides and complexity of the characters making them dimensional however much I thought there were characters labelled as good or bad for the reader.<br /><br />I go on and on about characters but they are the ones that drive and provide you with the twists and turns in the plot; they are unpredictable in their actions and behaviour. Even new additions to the story are unpredictable and have meaning to what they do/have done. It’s best to keep you’re emotions locked up because hate can go along way with such a book as this. However I give you permission to harness that hate for the end of the book because it leaves you on a cliffhanger that will have you regretting picking up this book so early from book three. I am eager to see what Ryan is able to do next in book three and I am positive that it will be better than both book one and two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8564193077307003244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1620013739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1620013739" />
    <a title="Sabrina Ye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33679484-sabrina-ye"><img alt="Sabrina Ye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570550546p2/33679484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_355068132" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/355068132" />
    <a title="Bern" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4789508-bern"><img alt="Bern" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463420514p2/4789508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/355068132?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bern" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bern" href="/user/show/4789508-bern">Bern</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=the-glorious-shelf-of-fabulousness">the-glorious-shelf-of-fabulousness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=insightful">insightful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=perfection">perfection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=loved-it-to-bits">loved-it-to-bits</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=epically-epic-epics">epically-epic-epics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355068132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6025989087769368722">You know, I'm not trying to get too deep or too emo-brooder here, but if you think about it, everybody kinda sucks in a way or another. I say this not because I'm trying to start some Freudian discussion on the depths of the human psyche, but because for once it actually pertains to what I'm about to say next (everybody quiet, lest I lose my train of thought and this all becomes useless):<br/><br/>All the characters in Spark can be some serious douchebags when they want to. Seriously. They'll torture, thr</span>
  <span id="freeText6025989087769368722" style="display:none">You know, I'm not trying to get too deep or too emo-brooder here, but if you think about it, everybody kinda sucks in a way or another. I say this not because I'm trying to start some Freudian discussion on the depths of the human psyche, but because for once it actually pertains to what I'm about to say next (everybody quiet, lest I lose my train of thought and this all becomes useless):<br /><br />All the characters in Spark can be some serious douchebags when they want to. Seriously. They'll torture, threaten, overthrow and God knows what else whoever comes in between them and their survival, and yet except for Kieran - whom I dislike intensely because I happen to loathe religious zealots - and some of his brainless followers, I loved every single character in this book. I feared for them, cheered for them, laughed when some of them tasered terrorists' balls and felt all sorts of emotions while engaged in reading Spark.<br /><br />I don't like doing synopsis when I feel like they won't be fair to the amazingness that the book was, so I'm just going to copy paste the synopsis GR has, as it is obviously quite fitting:<br /><br /><b>Waverly and Kieran are finally reunited on the Empyrean. Kieran has led the boys safely up to this point, and now that the girls are back, their mission seems slightly less impossible: to chase down the New Horizon, and save their parents from the enemy ship. But nothing is truly as it seems…Kieran’s leadership methods have raised Seth’s hackles— and Waverly’s suspicions. Is this really her fiancé? The handsome, loving boy she was torn from just a short time before? More and more, she finds her thoughts aligned with Seth’s. But if Seth is Kieran’s Enemy No. 1, what does that make her? <br /><br />In one night, a strange explosion rocks the Empyrean—shooting them off course and delaying their pursuit of the New Horizon—and Seth is mysteriously released from the brig. Seth is the most obvious suspect for the explosion, and Waverly the most obvious suspect for releasing him. As the tension reaches a boiling point, will Seth be able to find the true culprit before Kieran locks them both away—or worse? Will Waverly follow her heart, even if it puts lives at risk? With the balance of power precarious and the clock ticking, every decision counts… every step brings them closer to a new beginning, or a sudden end...</b><br /><br />Here I urge you: go read this series. Like, <i>now</i>. This has romance, sci-fi, political intrigue, action and suspense, so if for some mad reason you feel like Amy Kathleen Ryan's Sky Chasers series isn't for you, well, you can go stand in the corner with the rest of the drama lovers - I hear you guys have a lot of fun squeeing over John Green and Nicholas Sparks (not that I have anything against them, they're both sexy specimens of writers and all, their books are just not my type).<br /><br />Spark had me turning pages faster even than Glow, and I can't wait to see what happens in Flame *squeals out*<br /><br /><b>Insane-Obsessive-Compulsive-Shipping-Time!</b><br /><br />Sometimes, you have so much fun with a book you just feel like shipping everyone with everyone else. Here's a moment I take to make up relationships that sorta-kinda make sense inside the story, but that would never happen in a billion years without a slight nudge from lil' ol' moi:<br /><br /><b>Seth and Harvey</b> - Seth is one sexy recovering sociopath, and his first action upon beginning his 12-step program was carrying Harvey all the way up the endless stairs to where he could get treated after someone bludgeoned him in the head. Hundreds of pages later, Harvey acts all coy around Seth, sending him shy smiles and other stuff that <i>obviously</i> mean he's so infatuated with Seth he can barely stop himself from imploding with pent-up passion. Oh, Harvey also tells him he's "too damn good-looking". See? This is <i>so</i> not wishful thinking of me!<br /><br />They would both work because: Well, duh, did you not read anything I just said? They can barely keep their hands off each other!<br /><br /><b>Seth and everything else, ever (including inanimated objects)</b> - Three words: sexy. recovering. sociopath. Admit it, you just felt the Earth swoon.<br /><br /><b>Waverly and Sarah</b> - Both these gals spent some quality time alone in the brig after Waverly refused to leave Sarah to rot alone there, even if just for a day. Did they spend their time playing poker or did something racier occur? The world may never know...<br /><br />They would both work because: They went through some pretty screwed up stuff together, what with having their eggs stolen from them at the same time and all. I hear that makes for exquisite bonding time.<br /><br />And last but not least...<br /><br /><b>Kieran and Sarek</b> - I don't really like Kieran (stop aiming shoes at me, I'm done reasserting that now, ok?) but he <i>did</i> declare his love for Sarek. He didn't mean it <i>that</i> way, of course... Or did he?<br /><br />They would both work because: Kieran sucks, so maybe he'll find someone to love and endure him on Sarek. Poor, poor little Sarek, if that is the case.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6025989087769368722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_308630525" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308630525" />
    <a title="Amber (Books of Amber)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4354836-amber-books-of-amber"><img alt="Amber (Books of Amber)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554889916p2/4354836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308630525?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber (Books of Amber)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber (Books of Amber)" href="/user/show/4354836-amber-books-of-amber">Amber (Books of Amber)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4354836-amber-books-of-amber?shelf=otp-alert">otp-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4354836-amber-books-of-amber?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308630525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14401881688154278214">I read Glow when I received it for review last year, and I adored it. I remember being slightly put off at the beginning because the characters lived in such a strange society, where teenagers could get married and everyone accepted and even pushed it. Because babies are important on a spaceship, y'all. <br/><br/>Anyway, this review will contain spoilers for Glow, because Spark is a sequel and I can't contain myself. In any case, go and read Glow if you think it sounds like your sort of thing. Like I said</span>
  <span id="freeText14401881688154278214" style="display:none">I read Glow when I received it for review last year, and I adored it. I remember being slightly put off at the beginning because the characters lived in such a strange society, where teenagers could get married and everyone accepted and even pushed it. Because babies are important on a spaceship, y'all. <br /><br />Anyway, this review will contain spoilers for Glow, because Spark is a sequel and I can't contain myself. In any case, go and read Glow if you think it sounds like your sort of thing. Like I said, I personally loved it, although it's definitely not for everyone due to the themes involved. <br /><br />On with the Spark review...<br /><br />Was anyone reading my status updates on Goodreads? If you are following me on my personal twitter account, then your whole timeline would have been filled up with my tweets as I read the last fifty pages of this novel. IT WAS AWESOME. And I went a little crazy. <br /><br />Spark picks up where Glow left off, with the girls back on the right spaceship but the adults still on the other one after being kidnapped. Kieran is still leading the ship (boo!) and Waverly is trying to lose herself in her new job as a mechanic. Seth was still in the brig, but someone lets him out and he turns into a runaway. As much of a runaway as you can be, that is, on a relatively small ship.<br /><br />If you've read my review of Glow, or have spoken with me about the book, then you'll know that I DESPISED Kieran in that book. He was the worst. And he still is. I still absolutely hate him, and I don't think anything could change that. He's still as controlling as ever, and he is NOT fit to be a leader because he makes such stupid decisions, and yet he wants to be in charge. Idiot. POWER HUNGRY MORON. Ehem. Yeah, I don't like him at all and I want to throw him off the ship so he suffocates out there.<br /><br />Waverly is as awesome as ever, though! I love that the author wrote her to be affected by her time on the other ship, because that's not something you just get over overnight. She's a badass, though, and definitely one of my female characters. She has MAJOR issues and flaws, which is also awesome because it means a) character growth and b) lots of interesting scenes. <br /><br />I also love Seth. I despised him at the beginning of the first book, but he really grew on me towards the end of it and I've come out of this one absolutely worshipping him. Well, not quite. But I do think he's an awesome character. Again with the flaws thing. I adore the character growth he's been put through, and there is still potential for me. He really came a long way in this book and EEP. I love him. Surprisingly, he has become the most level headed out of the three main protagonists. <br /><br />Is the third book going to be the final one? Because at the end of Spark it says "Check out the third book in the series at such-and-such a date", but it didn't say "the third and final book". Does anybody know? <br /><br />If it IS the final book and this is just a trilogy, then I really hope that minimal amounts of time are spent talking about Waverly's love for Kieran. Because no. I don't like it, and really she should be well over him by now because he's an ass. <br /><br />This book is action packed, and while some found the pacing to be a little off, I thought it was fantastic. It reached its peak at about 65% - 70% of the way through, like most books do, and then shit just gets crazy. <br /><br />-----------------<br /><br />I HAVE SO MANY FEELINGS RIGHT NOW AND I DONT KNOW HOW TO TELL YOU GUYS<br /><br />IN SHORT:<br />- KIERAN IS STILL AN ASS, THAT IS NEVER GOING TO CHANGE<br />- WAVERLY IS A HBIC<br />- SETH IS AWESOME AND IS CLEARLY GOING TO BE THE HERO IN BOOK THREE BECAUSE HE'S THE BESTEST<br />- I AM A SOBBING MESS RIGHT NOW BECAUSE OF THAT ENDING<br />- IT WAS WRITTEN FLAWLESSLY<br />- FOUR FOR YOU, AMY KATHLEEN RYAN<br />- YOU GUYS ARE SO LUCKY YOU DONT FOLLOW ME ON MY PERSONAL TWITTER ACCOUNT BECAUSE I JUST HAD A MAJOR BREAKDOWN<br />- I DONT THINK THAT BREAKDOWN HAS FINISHED HAPPENING<br />- I AM NOT OK RIGHT NOW<br />- NOT<br />- OKAY<br />- GET ME BOOK THREE<br />- DEAD<br /><br />----<br /><br />FULL (AND HOPEFULLY MORE COHERENT) REVIEW TO FOLLOW SHORTLY ONCE I HAVE CLIMBED UP TEN STORIES TO FIND MY OXYGEN<br /><br />-----------------<br /><br />So. Yes. If you can't tell already, then I do recommend this book. *happy dance* And now I just have to wait for book three. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14401881688154278214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_302139050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302139050" />
    <a title="Tara Hall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4542501-tara-hall"><img alt="Tara Hall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447550939p2/4542501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/302139050?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara Hall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara Hall" href="/user/show/4542501-tara-hall">Tara Hall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542501-tara-hall?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542501-tara-hall?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542501-tara-hall?shelf=recommended-for-teens">recommended-for-teens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer302139050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer812679350803902278">More than a worthy sequel to Glow, it surpasses the first book in the series in plot, character realism and development , and in theme. The action is surprising and suspenseful, the romance is downplayed and believable, and the story is like a roller coaster ride. <br/><br/>The themes remain the same but more deeply explored, especially in the dynamics between Kieran and Seth. They steal the show in this book, especially Seth as we finally get to spend some real time in his head. He's a compelling narrato</span>
  <span id="freeText812679350803902278" style="display:none">More than a worthy sequel to Glow, it surpasses the first book in the series in plot, character realism and development , and in theme. The action is surprising and suspenseful, the romance is downplayed and believable, and the story is like a roller coaster ride. <br /><br />The themes remain the same but more deeply explored, especially in the dynamics between Kieran and Seth. They steal the show in this book, especially Seth as we finally get to spend some real time in his head. He's a compelling narrator, self-deprecating but not obnoxiously so, funny at times, but always clever and complex. Kieran really begins to grow as he reexamines his choices and his situation. Waverly takes a back seat to them, but the way she deals with her trauma, and then finally how she shocks the reader and herself with the results, bring her back to the forefront. <br /><br />Ryan's style manages to be fast-paced and readable enough for her age group, but she doesn't skimp on the details or the complexity. She is not afraid to hurt her characters, or to help them. You won't expect what's coming next. <br /><br />Not to be missed, this is already a favorite of this year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="812679350803902278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_249814724" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/249814724" />
    <a title="Taschima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2435020-taschima"><img alt="Taschima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574541558p2/2435020.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_466064827" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/466064827" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/138405-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425119034p2/138405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/466064827?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/138405-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138405-andrew?shelf=my-everything">my-everything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138405-andrew?shelf=jahwohl">jahwohl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138405-andrew?shelf=kvelling-for-ya">kvelling-for-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138405-andrew?shelf=actually-crazy">actually-crazy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138405-andrew?shelf=jesus-christ">jesus-christ</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138405-andrew?shelf=tabarnak">tabarnak</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138405-andrew?shelf=space-omfg">space-omfg</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer466064827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17681927044565885801">(Disclaimer: I'm writing this review before I've even written one for <i>Glow</i>. I make a lot of sense.)<br/><br/>Are you ready for a book that's lighthearted, feel-good to the brim, cup runneth over with kittens, puppies and stickers that say meow and paw princess, and ends on a happy note?<br/><br/>Well find another book, bitches, because this isn't it.<br/><br/>In Spark, you get none of those things, instead, you get a down payment for the carnage and chaos that will be sure to envelop <i>Flame</i>, the next (and possibly last and mo</span>
  <span id="freeText17681927044565885801" style="display:none">(Disclaimer: I'm writing this review before I've even written one for <i>Glow</i>. I make a lot of sense.)<br /><br />Are you ready for a book that's lighthearted, feel-good to the brim, cup runneth over with kittens, puppies and stickers that say meow and paw princess, and ends on a happy note?<br /><br />Well find another book, bitches, because this isn't it.<br /><br />In Spark, you get none of those things, instead, you get a down payment for the carnage and chaos that will be sure to envelop <i>Flame</i>, the next (and possibly last and most likely batshit bonkers) book in this series. But I'm not here to talk about Flame (unless Amy Kathleen Ryan would like to send me an ARC *wink wink /eyelashes get stuck together because those long things should never be winked/*). I'm here to talk about S P A R K / C H I S P A / 火花 / 불꽃 / شرارة / picture_of_me_in_my_backyard_flinting_a_rock_and_expressing_glee_at_that_SPARK.jpg<br /><br />One month after the events of Glow, the characters continue to evolve into people beyond what their young ages should ever have to experience (nbd). <br /><br /><i>Spark</i> finds Kieran grasping to power and using religious mandate to justify, to himself, why he should be the sole leader of the Empyrean. After having tasted the Kool-Aid and rejecting it because it's lime instead of cherry flavored (food coloring only does so much. Nice try, K), Kieran's support base has eroded and the only kids who attend services now are the ones obsessed with tambourines, creating models of baby Jesus in the manger with regurgitated french toast, and the kids who have discovered data dots with Kid Rock and ICP music videos on them and decide they need God in their life to get over it. Even Kieran's trusted aide-de-camp, Arthur, is beginning to see the writing on the wall: Kieran's hungry leadership style will not be compatible with his moral system.<br /><br />Waverly isn't having a blast either. You'd figure the girl who took a bullet to save her fellow captives would be honored with a parade with a wonky looking yet well-meaning float in her image, a procession of handsome, well-mannered (yet DTF) eligible bachelors, and free banana pancakes for the rest of her lyfe but no. While the older girls have Waverly's back and are <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1v6l82yuUk4" rel="nofollow noopener">G4L</a>, most of the younger girls have drunk the lime flavored Kool-Aid and LIKED IT and the blame for the failure of bringing their parents back is pinned on Waverly.<br /><br />The division between her and Kieran only increases as Kieran fits into the Anne Mather mold more and more. As time goes on, this spurs her into action leading to some of the tensest and most political scenes of the series so far.<br /><br />Seth, (one more person, I'M NOT DONE YET, stop rushing me ogm) now persona non grata, takes advantage of mysterious circumstances which allow him to escape the brig. On the lam from Kieran and his adjuncts, Seth finds himself Public Enemy #1 when he's accused of committing crimes he didn't commit. You're probably thinking, "um, what are you talking about, Seth was conniving and ruthless when he commanded the Empyrean, how could he not be committing crimes left and right, Kathryn Bigelow has even signed on to make the movie about his eventual death." It turns out the brig is good for a lot of things other than keeping borderline sociopaths separated from the general public, starvation diets, and allowing for a place for Seth to write his own personal <i>Mein Kampf</i>; it allows for self-reflection. Which, I might add, Seth has done a lot of, and it shows because qurlfrend has simmered down and is stealthily stomping around the Empyrean like a disgraced Dolce &amp; Gabbana model. What end is in store for Seth??? Read Spark. Find out for yourself. Go on. I'm right here. I'll wait. *drives off as soon as you turn around*<br /><br />--<br /><br />One of my favorite things about Spark (and this series) is how the characters continue to be unnervingly convincing. <br /><br />Kieran, for example, is fascinating (though still an ass) to watch because his speeches so mirror (even down to the mannerisms) those delivered by modern day televangelists. Also fascinating are the secondary characters; Marjorie, for example, assigns blame on Waverly over the failed rescue of their parents. Though Marjorie is misguided in her hate, she cannot help being affected by the traumas she has endured. And once again, Anne Mather shines, not because she's a shining paradigm of grandmotherly love, hair braiding skills, and democratic leadership, but because underneath her antagonism, there is a woman afraid that everything she has done for the survival of her ship will have been for naught and nullified with the thing she dreads most of all, being considered the first war criminal of New Earth. <br /><br />It's the staggering dimensionality of the characters of Spark and the tight plotting which continue to make the series so incredible. And these are the things I'll miss once the series comes to its conclusion.<br /><br />Now about the final moments of the bewk:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Waverly going down to the brig to save Seth / Waverly clinging to consciousness and using all her might to get there / the general feeling that she could actually die / Seth being the one to save her in the end / the general feeling that they could BOTH die / Sarah &amp; Sarek / Seth staying behind on the Empyrean<br /><br />ALL THESE THINGS GAVE ME FEELINGS.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17681927044565885801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_424777645" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/424777645" />
    <a title="VaultOfBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3929792-vaultofbooks"><img alt="VaultOfBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348989948p2/3929792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/424777645?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="VaultOfBooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="VaultOfBooks" href="/user/show/3929792-vaultofbooks">VaultOfBooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer424777645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1864615763411842957">By Amy Kathleen Ryan. Grade B+.<br/>When I received the book in the mail, I was quite excited to read it. For the cover itself had held me hostage; I found it captivating and entirely brilliantly designed. But I wasn’t aware of the fact that it is the second book in the Sky Chasers series. So, obviously when I started the book it was as if I had skipped a good half of it and had a lot of trouble making sense of what was going on.<br/><br/>Spark<br/>Waverly and Kieran are finally reunited on the Empyrean. Kieran has</span>
  <span id="freeText1864615763411842957" style="display:none">By Amy Kathleen Ryan. Grade B+.<br />When I received the book in the mail, I was quite excited to read it. For the cover itself had held me hostage; I found it captivating and entirely brilliantly designed. But I wasn’t aware of the fact that it is the second book in the Sky Chasers series. So, obviously when I started the book it was as if I had skipped a good half of it and had a lot of trouble making sense of what was going on.<br /><br />Spark<br />Waverly and Kieran are finally reunited on the Empyrean. Kieran has led the boys safely up to this point, and now that the girls are back, their mission seems slightly less impossible: to chase down the New Horizon, and save their parents from the enemy ship. But nothing is truly as it seems…Kieran’s leadership methods have raised Seth’s hackles— and Waverly’s suspicions. Is this really her fiancé? The handsome, loving boy she was torn from just a short time before? More and more, she finds her thoughts aligned with Seth’s. But if Seth is Kieran’s Enemy No. 1, what does that make her? <br />In one night, a strange explosion rocks the Empyrean—shooting them off course and delaying their pursuit of the New Horizon—and Seth is mysteriously released from the brig. Seth is the most obvious suspect for the explosion, and Waverly the most obvious suspect for releasing him. As the tension reaches a boiling point, will Seth be able to find the true culprit before Kieran locks them both away—or worse? Will Waverly follow her heart, even if it puts lives at risk? With the balance of power precarious and the clock ticking, every decision counts… every step brings them closer to a new beginning, or a sudden end…<br /> <br />The book is about two ships which are headed across the universe toward the New Earth (it is after our present Earth becomes a desolate desert, practically incapable of sustaining life). Two of our main characters, Seth and Max, are released from prison. Seth knows that they were set up for the sabotage aboard the ship. When it is discovered that someone from the New Horizon may have stowed away, Waverly, our female protagonist, is accused of allowing the enemy on-board and Seth is accused of helping her. Time passes and the Empyrean is no closer to rescuing the adults from the New Horizon. But terrorist attacks, murder, and distrust are now all over the place. Waverly copes with mechanical problems on the machinery just to avoid the accusatory stares of the others who blame her for their parents being left behind when they escaped.<br />Everyone wrongly blamed her for abandoning their parents, even though none of them would’ve made it out alive if she hadn’t done what she had. She had to live with everyone’s hatred and guilt everyday, but she still stayed strong and more clear-minded at the painfully young age of fifteen. I felt pity for her, and was immensely impressed by Ryan’s characterization.<br />Talking about the characters, I think all the characters have been described deftly but after a while Seth became my favourite. Since everyone hates him, and he admits of doing cruel things, I have to assume that Kieran was the hero in the first book. However, I still think Seth was the most level headed character in the whole book. And I really hope he is the hero in the next book.<br />Kieran, unfortunately, wasn’t as likable. He has no conscience, he is too controlling and takes stupid decisions. More than the safety of the people on the ship, he wants to safeguard his position as the Captain. Apart from this, I have to hand it to the author that she has come up with an ingeniously creative plot, and the characters make for a fresh change. They are not perfect, but so humanly flawed that you can empathize with them.<br />Overall, I really liked the story line and the characters and the easy flow of the story. Ryan’s writing style was commendable. The book is a real page turner and neither the story nor the characters are predictable, especially in the end. I highly recommend the book to YA lovers. I can’t wait for the next book to come out.<br /><br /><br />Originally reviewed at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.vaultofbooks.com">www.vaultofbooks.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1864615763411842957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_261317540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/261317540" />
    <a title="Jennifer Rinehart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3652157-jennifer-rinehart"><img alt="Jennifer Rinehart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442512260p2/3652157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/261317540?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Rinehart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Rinehart" href="/user/show/3652157-jennifer-rinehart">Jennifer Rinehart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3652157-jennifer-rinehart?shelf=books-i-d-read-again">books-i-d-read-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261317540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12048406156166196787">This book made me mad.<br/><br/>If you read the first book, you already know the premise of this story and where it left off with Kieran, Seth and Waverly. You know why the New Horizon attacked, you know what they wanted with all the girls from the Empyrean (nope, not a girl band or fashion advice) and you know what lengths Waverly went to to escape and to rescue the adults who were kidnapped along with the all the other girls.<br/><br/>You also should know what happened on the Empyrean with the boys, while the gir</span>
  <span id="freeText12048406156166196787" style="display:none">This book made me mad.<br /><br />If you read the first book, you already know the premise of this story and where it left off with Kieran, Seth and Waverly. You know why the New Horizon attacked, you know what they wanted with all the girls from the Empyrean (nope, not a girl band or fashion advice) and you know what lengths Waverly went to to escape and to rescue the adults who were kidnapped along with the all the other girls.<br /><br />You also should know what happened on the Empyrean with the boys, while the girls were living through their enforced baby machine drama, which is good because I don't want to summarize all of that.<br /><br />I have just one overwhelming feeling about this book and it is anger. I got so mad, gripping the pages, that I crumpled the paperback edges (I have a soft cover Advance Reader copy instead of the hardback that you see in the store) as I feverishly whipped through the chapters. I'm not sure that I've ever gotten this ticked off over a book, I'd blame it on my monthly, but it's the wrong time, this story just pushed my buttons, all of them!<br /><br />Here, in no real order of importance is what made me spark with rage:<br /><br />1. Blame - There's a lot to go around and no one's immune, not least of all Waverly. But the fact that so many of the kids on the Empryean blame her for not rescuing their parents is absurd and wrong, the girl got shot on her way back to the shuttle, one second later and she'd have died. Disgusting graffiti pops up in the corridors as many of the kids lump Waverly in with everything else that goes wrong on the ship. Arrgh, people being unjustly accused always rubs me the wrong way, but being blamed for not getting their parents out (throws arms up in exasperation!), well, it makes me doubly mad.<br /><br />2. Kieren - He was a sweet golden boy in the first book, a real helpful eagle scout type but this time around he is super different. There is still Kieran, hardworking and detail oriented, but he's arrogant enough to believe that his decisions are always best and that everyone should defer to him because he's fated to lead them. With his weirdy religious cult following him around, it isn't surprising that in this vacuum of real evaluation, he believes he's being objective and just, especially when he starts to hate on Waverly and even has her arrested for daring to speak out against his decisions.<br /><br />3. Seth - All the time in the brig has led to a lot of introspection. He can't go back in time to change things, but he knows he has to try to change his future, it's just that no one will give him a chance. Worst of all, tragedy is looming and the one person who could help avert it will not listen to him, not even a tiny bit and he has some seriously important info. So amidst his wallowing, there's a terrible sense of urgency, he has to succeed with this one thing or so many others will die.<br /><br />Don't read past this point if you don't want to read spoilers.<br /><br />SERIOUSLY! JUST DON'T.<br /><br />4. Jacob - the stowaway with the heart of a determined serial killer. Once the saboteur is revealed, you'd think there'd be a denouement, 'Oh golly, Seth, I'm so sorry that I thought you were working with this creepy dude, lets start a bromance now.' But capturing Jacob ends up not accomplishing much of anything but to create a futher rift between Kieran and the elected council led by Waverly.<br /><br />5. Or my number one reason to get royally mad: Anne Mather. When Kieran flies over to the New Horizon to negotiate a peace and trade for release of the hostages with Mather, I hoped this might be the end of the violence. Wow, so so wrong, because I forgot one inescapable detail about Mather; she's freaking evil! She's also totally smart, like Sherlock Holmes, an evil Sherlock (I guess that would be Dr. Moriarty) and she has a plan that totally trumps the one that Waverly came up with to free the hostages. The way she invites Kieran onto the ship, with music, a feast and applause, was hideously wrong and Kieran rightly recognized it for what it was, a ploy to keep him off balance. She honestly seemed to think a cup of tea with a few cookies would smooth things out.<br /><br />I guess in the end that's what really burned me, Anne Mather and her henchmen seem to think that a 'oh, sorry about murdering your parents and nearly destroying the only home you've ever known, we good now?' is enough to set the scales back to equal.<br /><br />I can't wait to read the next book, I have so many unanswered questions. I wonder if I'll be mad about it too.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12048406156166196787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
